this method performs the formula \textquotesingle{}abs(this) == abs(ss2)\textquotesingle{} and returns the result

(in other words it treats \textquotesingle{}this\textquotesingle{} and \textquotesingle{}ss2\textquotesingle{} as values without a sign) we don\textquotesingle{}t check the NaN flag \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a2c2c7de54743b12c05f1bfea7b153eba}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a2c2c7de54743b12c05f1bfea7b153eba} 
\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!Exp@{Exp}}
\index{Exp@{Exp}!ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Exp()}{Exp()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Exp (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$ \&}]{x }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Exponent this = exp(x) = e\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}x

we\textquotesingle{}re using the fact that our value is stored in form of\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}x = mantissa * 2^exponent
\end{DoxyVerb}
 then \begin{DoxyVerb}e^x = e^(mantissa* 2^exponent) or
e^x = (e^mantissa)^(2^exponent)
\end{DoxyVerb}
 \textquotesingle{}Exp\textquotesingle{} returns a carry if we can\textquotesingle{}t count the result (\textquotesingle{}x\textquotesingle{} is too big) \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a4c57d905ba44c691e1ed532753423e66}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a4c57d905ba44c691e1ed532753423e66}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ExpSurrounding0()}{ExpSurrounding0()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Exp\+Surrounding0 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$ \&}]{x,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{steps = {\ttfamily 0} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [private]}}

Exponent this = exp(x) = e\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}x where x is in (-\/1,1)

we\textquotesingle{}re using the formula exp(x) = 1 + (x)/(1!) + (x\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}2)/(2!) + (x\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}3)/(3!) + ... \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a961c89a45552dfac6d4a47e6e6d21106}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a961c89a45552dfac6d4a47e6e6d21106}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+From\+Double (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{value }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

this method converts from standard double into this class

standard double means IEEE-\/754 floating point value with 64 bits it is as follows (from \href{http://www.psc.edu/general/software/packages/ieee/ieee.html}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+psc.\+edu/general/software/packages/ieee/ieee.\+html}})\+:

The IEEE double precision floating point standard representation requires a 64 bit word, which may be represented as numbered from 0 to 63, left to right. The first bit is the sign bit, S, the next eleven bits are the exponent bits, \textquotesingle{}E\textquotesingle{}, and the final 52 bits are the fraction \textquotesingle{}F\textquotesingle{}\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}S EEEEEEEEEEE FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
0 1        11 12                                                63
\end{DoxyVerb}
 The value V represented by the word may be determined as follows\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If E=2047 and F is nonzero, then V=NaN ("{}\+Not a number"{})
\item If E=2047 and F is zero and S is 1, then V=-\/Infinity
\item If E=2047 and F is zero and S is 0, then V=Infinity
\item If 0\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}E\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}2047 then V=(-\/1)\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}S \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (E-\/1023) \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (1.\+F) where "{}1.\+F"{} is intended to represent the binary number created by prefixing F with an implicit leading 1 and a binary point.
\item If E=0 and F is nonzero, then V=(-\/1)\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}S \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (-\/1022) \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (0.\+F) These are "{}unnormalized"{} values.
\item If E=0 and F is zero and S is 1, then V=-\/0
\item If E=0 and F is zero and S is 0, then V=0 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a448d79907dbc27e897d0f6c55ecde0b4}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a448d79907dbc27e897d0f6c55ecde0b4} 
\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!FromFloat@{FromFloat}}

a method for converting a string into its value

it returns 1 if the value is too big -- we cannot pass it into the range of our class Big$<$exp,man$>$ (or if the base is incorrect)

that means only digits before the comma operator can make this value too big, all digits after the comma we can ignore

\textquotesingle{}source\textquotesingle{} -\/ pointer to the string for parsing

if \textquotesingle{}after\+\_\+source\textquotesingle{} is set that when this method finishes it sets the pointer to the new first character after parsed value

\textquotesingle{}value\+\_\+read\textquotesingle{} -\/ if the pointer is provided that means the value\+\_\+read will be true only when a value has been actually read, there can be situation where only such a string \textquotesingle{}-\/\textquotesingle{} or \textquotesingle{}+\textquotesingle{} will be parsed -- \textquotesingle{}after\+\_\+source\textquotesingle{} will be different from \textquotesingle{}source\textquotesingle{} but no value has been read (there are no digits) on other words if \textquotesingle{}value\+\_\+read\textquotesingle{} is true -- there is at least one digit in the string \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_ac33449ca94ff43cb02dde88ab6f3a18a}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_ac33449ca94ff43cb02dde88ab6f3a18a}

an auxiliary method for converting from a string \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a812ba4f542593e06097fea64055d18e8}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a812ba4f542593e06097fea64055d18e8} 
\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!IsInf@{IsInf}}
\index{IsInf@{IsInf}!ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{IsInf()}{IsInf()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Is\+Inf (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{float}]{value }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [private]}}

an auxiliary method to check if the float value is +/-\/infinity we provide this method because isinf(float) in only in C99 language

description taken from\+: \href{http://www.psc.edu/general/software/packages/ieee/ieee.php}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+psc.\+edu/general/software/packages/ieee/ieee.\+php}}

The IEEE single precision floating point standard representation requires a 32 bit word, which may be represented as numbered from 0 to 31, left to right. The first bit is the sign bit, S, the next eight bits are the exponent bits, \textquotesingle{}E\textquotesingle{}, and the final 23 bits are the fraction \textquotesingle{}F\textquotesingle{}\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}S EEEEEEEE FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
0 1      8 9                    31
\end{DoxyVerb}
 The value V represented by the word may be determined as follows\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If E=255 and F is nonzero, then V=NaN ("{}\+Not a number"{})
\item If E=255 and F is zero and S is 1, then V=-\/Infinity
\item If E=255 and F is zero and S is 0, then V=Infinity
\item If 0\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}E\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}255 then V=(-\/1)\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}S \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (E-\/127) \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (1.\+F) where "{}1.\+F"{} is intended to represent the binary number created by prefixing F with an implicit leading 1 and a binary point.
\item If E=0 and F is nonzero, then V=(-\/1)\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}S \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (-\/126) \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (0.\+F) These are "{}unnormalized"{} values.
\item If E=0 and F is zero and S is 1, then V=-\/0
\item If E=0 and F is zero and S is 0, then V=0 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_ac3a17607588c394ee7fa674e83f0d54a}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_ac3a17607588c394ee7fa674e83f0d54a} 
\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!IsInfoBit@{IsInfoBit}}
\index{IsInfoBit@{IsInfoBit}!ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item asm\+\_\+vc\+\_\+32 -\/ with asm code designed for Microsoft Visual C++ (32 bits)
\item asm\+\_\+gcc\+\_\+32 -\/ with asm code designed for GCC (32 bits)
\item asm\+\_\+vc\+\_\+64 -\/ with asm for VC (64 bit)
\item asm\+\_\+gcc\+\_\+64 -\/ with asm for GCC (64 bit)
\item no\+\_\+asm\+\_\+32 -\/ pure C++ version (32 bit) -\/ without any asm code
\item no\+\_\+asm\+\_\+64 -\/ pure C++ version (64 bit) -\/ without any asm code 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_ae6addbbd86cd8b9ed60d0afc8c80181c}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_ae6addbbd86cd8b9ed60d0afc8c80181c} 
\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!Ln@{Ln}}
\index{Ln@{Ln}!ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Ln()}{Ln()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Ln (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$ \&}]{x }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Natural logarithm this = ln(x) (a logarithm with the base equal \textquotesingle{}e\textquotesingle{})

we\textquotesingle{}re using the fact that our value is stored in form of\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}x = mantissa * 2^exponent
\end{DoxyVerb}
 then \begin{DoxyVerb}ln(x) = ln (mantissa * 2^exponent) = ln (mantissa) + (exponent * ln (2))
\end{DoxyVerb}
 the mantissa we\textquotesingle{}ll show as a value from range \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}1,2) because the logarithm is decreasing too fast when \textquotesingle{}x\textquotesingle{} is going to 0

return values\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 0 -\/ ok
\item 1 -\/ overflow (carry)
\item 2 -\/ incorrect argument (x\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}=0) 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_aef21587e553d4e051279ba87812f21f0}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_aef21587e553d4e051279ba87812f21f0}

\index{LnSurrounding1@{LnSurrounding1}!ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{LnSurrounding1()}{LnSurrounding1()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Ln\+Surrounding1 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$ \&}]{x,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{steps = {\ttfamily 0} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [private]}}

Natural logarithm this = ln(x) where x in range \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}1,2)

we\textquotesingle{}re using the formula\+: ln x = 2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} \mbox{[} (x-\/1)/(x+1) + (1/3)((x-\/1)/(x+1))\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}3 + (1/5)((x-\/1)/(x+1))\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}5 + ... \mbox{]} \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a6a50f7bec2c05935c06bbe1dd43fa4ac}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a6a50f7bec2c05935c06bbe1dd43fa4ac}

Logarithm from \textquotesingle{}x\textquotesingle{} with a \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{}

we\textquotesingle{}re using the formula\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}Log(x) with 'base' = ln(x) / ln(base)
\end{DoxyVerb}
 return values\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 0 -\/ ok
\item 1 -\/ overflow
\item 2 -\/ incorrect argument (x\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}=0)
\item 3 -\/ incorrect base (a\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}=0 or a=1) 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_abdd4b5bd37f010f2c3dc6e770827693d}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_abdd4b5bd37f010f2c3dc6e770827693d} 
\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!Mod@{Mod}}
\index{Mod@{Mod}!ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Mod()}{Mod()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Mod (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$ \&}]{ss2 }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

caltulate the remainder from a division

samples
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 12.\+6 mod 3 = 0.\+6 because 12.\+6 = 3\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}4 + 0.\+6
\item -\/12.\+6 mod 3 = -\/0.\+6 bacause -\/12.\+6 = 3\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}(-\/4) + (-\/0.\+6)
\item 12.\+6 mod -\/3 = 0.\+6
\item -\/12.\+6 mod -\/3 = -\/0.\+6
\end{DoxyItemize}

in other words\+: this(old) = ss2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} q + this(new)

return value\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 0 -\/ ok
\item 1 -\/ carry
\item 2 -\/ improper argument (ss2 is zero) 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_ab60bb059c684494fd91bb9d257ebd9c6}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_ab60bb059c684494fd91bb9d257ebd9c6}

this method does the half-\/to-\/even rounding (banker\textquotesingle{}s rounding)

if is\+\_\+half is\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item true -\/ that means the rest was equal the half (0.\+5 decimal)
\item false -\/ that means the rest was greater than a half (greater than 0.\+5 decimal)
\end{DoxyItemize}

if the rest was less than a half then don\textquotesingle{}t call this method (the rounding should does nothing then) \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_add0ae88434679a663de0f5b3822d0146}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_add0ae88434679a663de0f5b3822d0146}

\index{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$@{ttmath::Big$<$ exp, man $>$}!SetLn10@{SetLn10}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{SetLn10()}{SetLn10()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Set\+Ln10 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

this method sets the value of ln(10) the natural logarithm from 10

I introduced this constant especially to make the conversion \doxylink{classttmath_1_1Big_a3d8da6a88dda87845a13a13c8abfcfa4}{To\+String()} being faster. In fact the method \doxylink{classttmath_1_1Big_a3d8da6a88dda87845a13a13c8abfcfa4}{To\+String()} is keeping values of logarithms it has calculated but it must calculate the logarithm at least once. If a program, which uses this library, is running for a long time this would be ok, but for programs which are running shorter, for example for CGI applications which only once are printing values, this would be much inconvenience. Then if we\textquotesingle{}re printing with base (radix) 10 and the mantissa of our value is smaller than or equal to TTMATH\+\_\+\+BUILTIN\+\_\+\+VARIABLES\+\_\+\+SIZE we don\textquotesingle{}t calculate the logarithm but take it from this constant. \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_ac34df29b0b14bee8687eefc07b8698af}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_ac34df29b0b14bee8687eefc07b8698af}

methods for comparing

this method performs the formula \textquotesingle{}abs(this) \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} abs(ss2)\textquotesingle{} and returns the result

(in other words it treats \textquotesingle{}this\textquotesingle{} and \textquotesingle{}ss2\textquotesingle{} as values without a sign) we don\textquotesingle{}t check the NaN flag \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a6a2dbb9846bbebd87393f2ea8f75911d}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a6a2dbb9846bbebd87393f2ea8f75911d}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Standardizing()}{Standardizing()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+Standardizing (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

this method moves all bits from mantissa into its left side (suitably changes the exponent) or if the mantissa is zero it sets the exponent to zero as well (and clears the sign bit and sets the zero bit)

it can return a carry the carry will be when we don\textquotesingle{}t have enough space in the exponent

you don\textquotesingle{}t have to use this method if you don\textquotesingle{}t change the mantissa and exponent directly \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_ab06fe23729905c90461b52be26104744}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_ab06fe23729905c90461b52be26104744}

an auxiliary method for converting into the string (when this is integer)

after floating point calculating the new mantissa can consist of some fraction so if our value is integer we should check the new mantissa (after the decimal point there should be only zeroes)

often this is a last digit different from zero To\+String\+\_\+\+Base\+Round would not get rid of it because the method make a test against an integer value (To\+String\+\_\+\+Round\+Mantissa\+Would\+Be\+Integer) and returns immediately \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_af2dfb541b7478793ade1114e83433c5f}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_af2dfb541b7478793ade1114e83433c5f}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} exp, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} man$>$ \\
template$<$class string\+\_\+type , class char\+\_\+type $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacettmath_a9897e861179132b64f0e2640dde9d7b7}{uint}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Big}{ttmath\+::\+Big}}$<$ exp, man $>$\+::\+To\+String\+\_\+\+Create\+New\+Mantissa\+And\+Exponent (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{string\+\_\+type \&}]{new\+\_\+man,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structttmath_1_1Conv}{Conv}} \&}]{conv,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classttmath_1_1Int}{Int}}$<$ exp+1 $>$ \&}]{new\+\_\+exp }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [private]}}

an auxiliary method for converting into the string

input\+: base -\/ the base in range \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}2,16\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}

output\+: return values\+: 0 -\/ ok 1 -\/ if there was a carry new\+\_\+man -\/ the new mantissa for \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{} new\+\_\+exp -\/ the new exponent for \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{}

mathematic part\+:

the value is stored as\+: value = mantissa \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent we want to show \textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{} as\+: value = new\+\_\+man \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp

then \textquotesingle{}new\+\_\+man\textquotesingle{} we\textquotesingle{}ll print using the standard method from UInt$<$$>$ type for printing and \textquotesingle{}new\+\_\+exp\textquotesingle{} is the offset of the comma operator in a system of a base \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{}

value = mantissa \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent value = mantissa \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp / base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp) value = mantissa \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent / base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp) \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp

look at the part (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent / base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp), there\textquotesingle{}ll be good if we take a \textquotesingle{}new\+\_\+exp\textquotesingle{} equal that value when the (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent / base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp) will be equal one

on account of the \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{} is not as power of 2 (can be from 2 to 16), this formula will not be true for integer \textquotesingle{}new\+\_\+exp\textquotesingle{} then in our case we take \textquotesingle{}base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp\textquotesingle{} {\itshape greater} than \textquotesingle{}2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent\textquotesingle{}

if \textquotesingle{}base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp\textquotesingle{} were smaller than \textquotesingle{}2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent\textquotesingle{} the new mantissa could be greater than the max value of the container \doxylink{classttmath_1_1UInt}{UInt$<$man$>$}

value = mantissa \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent / base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp) \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp let M = mantissa \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent / base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp) then value = M \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp

in our calculation we treat M as floating value showing it as\+: M = mm \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}ee where ee will be \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}= 0

next we\textquotesingle{}ll move all bits of mm into the right when ee is equal zero abs(ee) must not be too big that only few bits from mm we can leave

then we\textquotesingle{}ll have\+: M = mmm \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}0 \textquotesingle{}mmm\textquotesingle{} is the new\+\_\+man which we\textquotesingle{}re looking for

new\+\_\+exp we calculate in this way\+: 2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}= base\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}new\+\_\+exp new\+\_\+exp \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= log base (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent) \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}-\/ logarithm with the base \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{} from (2\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}exponent)

but we need new\+\_\+exp as integer then we test\+: if new\+\_\+exp is greater than zero and with fraction we add one to new\+\_\+exp new\+\_\+exp = new\+\_\+exp + 1 (if new\+\_\+exp\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0 and with fraction) and at the end we take the integer part\+: new\+\_\+exp = int(new\+\_\+exp) \Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_aa751d8c162c11bce4a65e7ef4e54aede}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_aa751d8c162c11bce4a65e7ef4e54aede}

a special method used to calculate the new mantissa and exponent when the \textquotesingle{}base\textquotesingle{} is equal 4, 8 or 16


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item when base is 4 then bits is 2
\item when base is 8 then bits is 3
\item when base is 16 then bits is 4 (and the algorithm can be used with a base greater than 16) 
\end{DoxyItemize}\Hypertarget{classttmath_1_1Big_a0d278481ee54274a828fae863cdf4e4a}\label{classttmath_1_1Big_a0d278481ee54274a828fae863cdf4e4a}
